## SLIDE 1: Title Slide
Visual Layout:
Background: Clean, professional gradient (dark navy blue fading to deep charcoal) OR solid dark background with subtle data flow pattern overlay

Logo: Expanso logo in top-left corner (standard positioning)

Primary Headline (Large, Bold, Center-Aligned):


The Upstream Data Platform That Cuts
Cloud Data Costs by 50â€“70%
Font: Sans-serif, bold weight, ~48-60pt
Color: White or bright cyan (high contrast)
Positioning: Upper third of slide, centered

Subheadline (Medium Weight, Directly Below):


Filter, transform, and govern data at the sourceâ€”
before it hits Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, or Datadog
Font: Sans-serif, regular or light weight, ~24-32pt
Color: Light gray or soft white (slightly muted vs. headline)
Positioning: Centered, 1-2 lines below headline

Optional Visual Element (Subtle, Non-Competing):
A simple, clean diagram showing data flow:



[Data Sources] â†’ [EXPANSO] â†’ [Platform Logos: Snowflake | Databricks | Splunk | Datadog]
                    â†“
             "50-70% Less Data"
Style: Minimalist line diagram, icons only, muted colors
Positioning: Center or lower-center of slide
Purpose: Reinforce spatial "upstream" concept without cluttering

Bottom Section (Standard Contact Info):


David Aronchick, CEO
aronchick@expanso.io
Font: Small (~14-16pt), light weight
Color: Medium gray
Positioning: Bottom-left or centered at bottom

Optional Tagline (Small, Subtle):


Expanso: Upstream Data Control
Font: ~12-14pt, light weight
Color: Muted gray
Positioning: Bottom-right corner
Purpose: Reinforce category positioning without overwhelming

Design Notes:
Color Palette:
Primary: Dark navy/charcoal background
Accent: Bright cyan or electric blue (for "Upstream" and key words)
Text: White (headlines), light gray (subtext)
Logos: Full color for platform logos (Snowflake, Databricks, etc.)
Typography Hierarchy:
Hero Statement: Largest, boldest ("The Upstream Data Platform...")
Value Prop: Medium, clear ("Filter, transform, govern...")
Contact: Smallest, unobtrusive
Visual Balance:
Top 40%: Headline + Subheadline
Middle 40%: Optional data flow diagram
Bottom 20%: Contact info + tagline
Why This Works:
âœ… Outcome-First
"50-70% cost reduction" immediately grabs CFO/FinOps attention

âœ… Spatial Positioning
"Upstream" + "before it hits" establishes your unique market position

âœ… Platform Name-Drops
Mentioning Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, Datadog:

Makes it immediately relevant to your ICP
Positions you as complementary (not competitive)
Creates pattern interrupt ("Wait, you work WITH Snowflake?")
âœ… Clean & Professional
No clutter, no jargon, no confusionâ€”just a clear value statement

Alternative Version (If Presenting to Technical Audience):
Primary Headline:



The Missing Control Layer in the Modern Data Stack
Subheadline:



Process data at the source. Cut volumes 50-70%.
Reduce platform costs. Automate compliance.
When to Use: Technical conferences, architect/engineer audiences, developer-focused events

When NOT to Use: Executive presentations, CFO/FinOps audiences (lead with business outcomes instead)

Presentation Tips:
Opening Line (When Presenting):
"Today I'm going to show you how to cut your cloud data costs by 50 to 70 percentâ€”without losing a single insight. We do this by controlling data upstream, before it hits your expensive platforms like Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, or Datadog."

Pause After Title Slide:
Let the "50-70%" number land. Don't rush to the next slide. This creates intrigue and gives the audience time to process the bold claim.

Transition to Slide 2:
"Now, I know what you're thinking: 'That sounds too good to be true.' So let me show you why your cloud bills keep growingâ€”and why traditional approaches can't fix it."

This slide sets the stage for your entire narrative: Problem â†’ Diagnosis â†’ Solution â†’ Proof.

Color Palette:
Background: Dark navy or charcoal (consistent with Slide 1)
Title: White or bright cyan
Diagram Elements:
Data sources: Light gray icons
Arrow: Bold white or cyan
"Unfiltered Data" box: Dark red or orange (warning color)
Dollar signs: Bright yellow or gold ($$$ = cost)
Platform logos: Full color
Key Messages: White text with accent colors on percentages
Stats Bar: Muted gray text
Why This Slide Works:
âœ… Visual Impact
The diagram immediately shows the problem: data flows unfiltered into expensive platforms

âœ… Concrete Numbers
"60-70%", "40% YoY", "$13M" make the pain tangible and measurable

âœ… Multi-Persona Appeal
CFO/FinOps: Sees cost problem (40% growth, $13M waste)
Data Engineers: Sees operational pain (40% time firefighting)
CDO: Sees strategic risk (unused data, no ROI)
âœ… Third-Party Validation
Gartner and CIO Dive citations prove this isn't just "your" problemâ€”it's industry-wide

âœ… Sets Up Your Solution
By showing data flowing FROM sources TO platforms, you're priming the audience for the "what if we controlled it BEFORE it arrives?" insight on Slide 3

Presentation Script (When Delivering This Slide):
Opening:
"Let me show you why your cloud bills keep growingâ€”and why you can't fix it with your current architecture."

Point to Diagram:
"Here's what's happening: All your dataâ€”from edge devices, servers, applications, IoT sensorsâ€”flows directly into your cloud platforms. [Pause] No filtering. No optimization. No control."

Point to Dollar Signs:
"And you pay at every stage: Ingestion costs. Storage costs. Compute costs. Egress costs. It's what we call the '$10M Data Tax.'"

Point to Key Messages:
"Here's the kicker: 60 to 70 percent of the data sitting in Snowflake is never queried. You're paying to store and process data you'll never use. [Pause]

Your Snowflake bill grows 40% year-over-year, but your insights don't. And your data teams? They spend 40% of their time firefighting broken pipelines instead of building new capabilities."

Point to Stats Bar:
"And this isn't just anecdotal. Gartner reports that data quality issues cost the average enterprise $13 million annually. CIO Dive found that 62% of enterprises report storage cost overruns. This is an industry-wide crisis."

Transition to Slide 3:
"So why does this happen? Because the modern data stack is missing a critical layer. Let me show you..."

Design Tips:
Keep It Simple:
Don't overload with too many icons or elements
The flow should be instantly readable: Sources â†’ Data â†’ Platforms â†’ $$$$
Use Animation (Optional):
If presenting live, consider simple animations:

Step 1: Show data sources
Step 2: Arrow appears with "100% Volume"
Step 3: Dollar signs multiply
Step 4: Platform logos appear
Step 5: Key messages fade in
Warning: Only use animation if presenting live. For PDF decks, use static version.

Make Platform Logos Recognizable:
Use the actual Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, Datadog logosâ€”your audience will immediately recognize them and think, "That's us!"

Alternative Version (More Empathy-Driven):
If you want to validate their past decisions first:

Title:


You've Done Everything Rightâ€”And Your Bills Still Doubled
Body:


âœ… You invested in best-in-class platforms
   [Logos: Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, Datadog]

âœ… You hired talented data teams

âœ… You centralized data for a "single source of truth"

âŒ But your cloud data bills grew 40% YoY

âŒ Your pipelines are brittle and break constantly

âŒ Your best engineers spend 60% of time firefighting
Bottom Line (Bold):


The problem isn't your tools. It's your architecture.
When to Use This Version:

Defensive audiences who've already invested heavily
Presentations to teams that might feel criticized
When you need to build trust before challenging their approach
Final Recommendation:
Use the diagram-focused version for most audiences. It's visual, clear, and immediately communicates the problem without words.

Save the empathy-driven version for audiences that might be defensive about their current stack.

Next Step: Slide 3 should introduce the root cause (downstream-only architecture) before Slide 4 introduces your solution category ("Upstream Data Control").


## SLIDE 3: The Root Cause
Slide Title (Bold, Top):


The Root Cause: Downstream-Only Architecture
Font: Sans-serif, bold, ~36-42pt
Color: White or bright accent color
Positioning: Top of slide, left-aligned or centered

Primary Message (Large, Centered):


For decades, best practice was:
Collect ALL data â†’ Move it to a central location â†’ Process it there

This made sense when data was small and centralized.

Today? It's the most expensive way to operate.
Font: Sans-serif, medium weight, ~22-26pt
Color: White with key phrases in accent color
Positioning: Upper-center of slide
Style: Clean line breaks, emphasize the OLD workflow

The Visual: Side-by-Side Comparison
Layout: "Then vs. Now"

Color Palette:
Background: Dark navy or charcoal (consistent with Slides 1-2)
Title: White or bright cyan
Body Text: White for main text
"NO CONTROL" Box: Dark red or orange background (warning/problem color)
Dollar Signs: Bright yellow/gold
Arrows: Bold white or cyan
Accent Text: Highlight key phrases ("most expensive", "Data Tax") in cyan or yellow
Why This Slide Works:
âœ… Validates the Past
"This made sense when data was small" â†’ You're not calling them stupid, you're saying the world changed

âœ… Identifies the Structural Problem
It's not about tools or peopleâ€”it's about architecture

âœ… Introduces "Data Tax" Concept
Memorable metaphor that you'll reference throughout the deck

âœ… Visual Simplicity
The "missing layer" diagram is instantly understandable

âœ… Sets Up Your Solution
By showing the GAP, you create the need for Slide 4 (introducing Expanso as the solution)

Presentation Script (When Delivering This Slide):
Opening:
"So why does this problem exist? It's not because you made bad decisions. It's because the architecture that worked for 20 years no longer works today."

Point to Message:
"For decades, best practice was simple: Collect all your data, move it to a central locationâ€”your data warehouse or data lakeâ€”and process it there. [Pause]

And that made perfect sense when data volumes were measured in gigabytes, when everything was centralized, and when you could predict your costs."

Transition to "Today":
"But today? Data volumes are measured in terabytes or petabytes. Data comes from everywhereâ€”edge devices, cloud applications, IoT sensors. And costs? They're completely unpredictable and growing 40% year-over-year."

Point to Diagram:
"Here's the structural problem: The modern data stack has no control layer. [Pause]

Data flows from your sources directly into expensive downstream platforms. There's no filtering. No optimization. No governance at the source. Everything just... moves."

Point to "Data Tax":
"And that means every single byte you touch forces you to pay what we call a 'Data Tax.' You pay to transfer it. You pay to store it. You pay to compute on it. Whether it's valuable or not."

Closing:
"By the time your data lands in Snowflake or Databricks, the financial damage is already done. You can't optimize your way out of this problem downstream. [Pause]

You need to solve it upstream."

Transition to Slide 4:
"So what's the solution? You need a control layerâ€”something that sits between your sources and your platforms. Let me show you what that looks like..."

Alternative Version: "The Belief vs. Reality" Framework

When to Use This Version:

More confrontational audiences who need to be challenged
Technical audiences who appreciate directness
When you want to create more cognitive dissonance
Design Tips:
Keep the Focus on Architecture, Not Tools:
Don't criticize Snowflake, Databricks, etc. directly
Frame it as: "These platforms are greatâ€”but they're downstream. The problem is upstream."
Use the "Missing Layer" Visual:
The gap in the architecture should be visually obvious
Use a red X or warning color to highlight the missing control layer
Emphasize the Inevitability:
"By the time data lands in the cloud, the damage is done" â†’ Creates urgency
Connect to Slide 2:
Reference the "$10M Data Tax" from Slide 2
Show that the root cause (no control layer) creates the symptoms (runaway costs)
Animation Options (If Presenting Live):
Step 1: Show "The Old World vs. Today" comparison
Step 2: Fade in the architecture diagram
Step 3: Highlight the "NO CONTROL" gap with red box
Step 4: Show dollar signs multiplying downstream
Step 5: Final message appears: "By the time data lands..."
Warning: Only use animation for live presentations. Static version for PDF decks.

Key Messaging Points:
âœ… DO Say:
"The architecture that worked for 20 years doesn't work today"
"The modern data stack is missing a control layer"
"Every byte you touch forces you to pay a Data Tax"
"By the time data lands downstream, the damage is done"
âŒ DON'T Say:
"Your tools are bad" (you need them as partners)
"You made the wrong decisions" (creates defensiveness)
"Just use less data" (oversimplifies the problem)
Transition to Slide 4:
This slide diagnoses the root cause (no control layer).

Slide 4 should introduce the solution category ("Upstream Data Control") before you introduce Expanso specifically.

The narrative arc is:

Slide 2: Problem (symptoms)
Slide 3: Root cause (diagnosis)
Slide 4: Solution category (new way of thinking)
Slide 5: Your product (Expanso as the definitive solution)
Would you like me to create Slide 4 now? (Introducing "Upstream Data Control" as the solution category)

## SLIDE 4: The Solution Category
Slide Title (Bold, Top):


The Solution: Upstream Data Control
Font: Sans-serif, bold, ~36-42pt
Color: Bright accent color (cyan/electric blue) to signal shift from problem to solution
Positioning: Top of slide, left-aligned or centered

Primary Message (Large, Centered):


Stop paying the Data Tax.

Control data BEFORE it hits expensive platformsâ€”

Why This Slide Works:
âœ… Introduces the Solution Category First
You're not selling Expanso yetâ€”you're selling the concept of upstream control

âœ… Visual Contrast
The before/after or flow diagram makes the solution instantly understandable

âœ… Shows the Mechanism
Three clear pillars (Filter, Transform, Govern) explain HOW it works

âœ… Quantifies the Outcome
"50-70% cost reduction" ties back to your opening promise

âœ… Multiplier Effect
"Filter once upstream â†’ Save everywhere downstream" shows compounding value

âœ… Sets Up Expanso
By establishing the category, Slide 5 can position Expanso as the definitive solution

Presentation Script (When Delivering This Slide):
Opening:
"So here's the solution: Upstream Data Control. [Pause]

Instead of moving all your data downstream and dealing with the consequences, you control it upstreamâ€”at the sourceâ€”before it ever hits your expensive platforms."

Point to Diagram:
"Here's what that looks like architecturally. Data still flows from your sourcesâ€”edge devices, cloud applications, IoT sensors. But now, there's a control layer sitting upstream."

Point to Three Pillars:
"This control layer does three things:

First, it filters. It eliminates 50 to 70 percent of the noiseâ€”duplicate events, unnecessary logs, data you'll never query. Only valuable data moves downstream.

Second, it transforms. It optimizes, enriches, and structures data before it moves. So when it arrives at Snowflake or Databricks, it's already ready to use. No more expensive compute just to clean your data.

Third, it governs. It detects PII, masks sensitive data, and enforces compliance policies at the source. Before data leaves your trusted environment."

Point to Outcome:
"The result? Instead of 100% of your data hitting expensive platforms, only 30% arrives. And that means 50 to 70 percent cost reduction."

Emphasize Multiplier Effect:
"And here's the kicker: You filter once upstream, and you save everywhere downstream. Snowflake gets less data. Databricks gets less data. Splunk gets less data. Datadog gets less data. S3 storage costs drop. Every platform in your stack becomes cheaper."

Transition to Slide 5:
"Now, this isn't theoretical. We've built this. It's called Expanso. Let me show you how it works..."

Design Tips:
Make the Control Layer Visually Distinct:
Use a bright accent color (cyan, green) to make it stand out
Add a subtle glow or border to emphasize it's the key innovation
Position it clearly BETWEEN sources and platforms
Show the Math:
"100% data â†’ 30% data = 70% savings" should be crystal clear
Use visual size differences (large arrow before, small arrow after)
Use Icons Consistently:

ğŸ”’ = Govern (throughout the deck)
This creates visual consistency and memory anchors
Emphasize "Before":

This reinforces your spatial positioning (upstream vs. downstream)

Typography & Hierarchy Guide:
Level 1: Title
Font Size: 36-42pt
Weight: Bold
Color: Bright cyan/electric blue
Purpose: Establish the category name
Level 2: Primary Message
Font Size: 24-28pt
Weight: Medium-bold
Color: White with accent highlights
Purpose: Core value proposition
Level 3: Diagram Labels
Font Size: 18-22pt
Weight: Regular
Color: White or light gray
Purpose: Explain the flow
Level 4: Pillar Details
Font Size: 16-20pt
Weight: Regular
Color: White
Purpose: Explain mechanisms
Level 5: Outcomes/Stats
Font Size: 20-24pt (larger than details)
Weight: Bold
Color: Bright accent (cyan, green, yellow)
Purpose: Highlight results
Spacing & Layout Guidelines:
Top Section (20%):
Title
Primary message
Middle Section (60%):
Main diagram showing control layer
Three pillars (Filter, Transform, Govern)
Bottom Section (20%):
Outcome statement
Optional proof points or callout box
Icon Usage Guide:
Consistent Icons Throughout Deck:
ğŸ” Filter = Magnifying glass (represents finding what matters)
âš¡ Transform = Lightning bolt (represents speed/power)
ğŸ”’ Govern = Lock (represents security/compliance)
âœ… Success = Checkmark (represents solution/positive outcome)
âŒ Problem = X mark (represents gap/issue)
ğŸ’° Cost = Dollar signs (represents financial impact)
Design Note: Consider replacing emoji with custom icons in your brand colors for a more professional look

Color Psychology Applied:
Problem Colors (Slides 2-3):
Red/Orange = Warning, cost, danger
Used for: "NO CONTROL", dollar signs (problem state)
Solution Colors (Slide 4+):
Cyan/Blue = Trust, intelligence, technology
Green = Success, savings, positive outcome
Used for: Control layer, checkmarks, savings
Neutral Colors:
Dark navy/charcoal = Background (professional, stable)
White/light gray = Text (clarity, readability)
Platform logos = Full color (recognition, partnership)
Mobile/Print Considerations:
If this deck will be:

Emailed as PDF: Ensure all text is readable at 50% zoom
Printed: Use high-contrast colors (avoid subtle grays)
Viewed on mobile: Keep text size 16pt minimum, avoid tiny icons
A/B Testing Recommendations:
If you're presenting to multiple audiences, test these variations:

Version A: Outcome-First
Lead with "50-70% cost reduction"
Show ROI math
Best for: CFO, FinOps, Economic Buyers
Version B: Architecture-First
Lead with "The missing layer in the modern data stack"
Show technical diagram
Best for: CTOs, Architects, Technical Champions
Version C: Problem-First
Lead with "Stop paying the Data Tax"
Emphasize pain points
Best for: VPs of Data, Platform Engineering Directors
Recommendation: Default to Version A (Outcome-First) for cold audiences, Version B (Architecture-First) for technical deep-dives

Slide 4 Summary:
Purpose: Establish "Upstream Data Control" as the solution category
Key Message: Control data BEFORE it hits expensive platforms
Visual Strategy: Show the control layer sitting between sources and platforms
Outcome: 50-70% cost reduction through intelligent filtering, transformation, and governance
Next Step: Slide 5 introduces Expanso as the definitive upstream data platform

What Makes This Slide Effective:
âœ… Category Creation
You're not just selling a productâ€”you're introducing a new way of thinking about data architecture

âœ… Visual Clarity
The diagram is instantly understandable: Sources â†’ Control â†’ Platforms

âœ… Three Mechanisms
Filter, Transform, Governâ€”clear, memorable, actionable

âœ… Quantified Value
50-70% isn't vagueâ€”it's tied to specific mechanisms (filtering volume)

âœ… Multiplier Effect
Shows why the savings are so dramatic (one filter saves across ALL platforms)

âœ… Platform-Agnostic
Works with Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, Datadogâ€”not replacing them

Common Questions This Slide Answers:
Q: "How is this different from ETL tools?"
A: Built into the slideâ€”"Transform intelligently BEFORE it moves" (not after)

Q: "Won't this add latency?"
A: Built into the slideâ€”"4x faster time-to-insight" (processing at source is faster)

Q: "Do we need to rip and replace our stack?"
A: Built into the slideâ€”Shows your platforms (â„ï¸ ğŸ§± ğŸ”¥ ğŸ¶) still in place

Q: "How much will this really save us?"
A: Built into the slideâ€”"Every GB filtered = $100+ saved"

Presentation Tips for This Slide:
Pace Yourself:
This is a critical pivot slideâ€”don't rush through it. Spend 2-3 minutes here.

Use the "Pause and Point" Technique:
Point to sources: "Data starts here..."
Point to control layer: "Now there's a control layer..."
Point to platforms: "So only valuable data arrives here..."
Point to outcome: "Result: 50 to 70 percent cost reduction"
Anticipate Skepticism:
If you see skeptical faces, address it directly:

"I know this sounds too good to be true. So let me show you exactly how we do this and prove it with real customer results..."

Then transition confidently to Slide 5.

â”‚  The Solution: Upstream Data Control                        â”‚
â”‚                                                              â”‚
â”‚  THE PROBLEM:                                               â”‚
â”‚  Traditional architectures move ALL data downstream first,   â”‚
â”‚  then try to optimize. By then, you've already paid the     â”‚
â”‚  Data Tax.                                                   â”‚
â”‚                                                              â”‚
â”‚  THE SOLUTION:                                              â”‚
â”‚  Introduce a control layer UPSTREAMâ€”at the sourceâ€”that:     â”‚
â”‚                                                              â”‚
â”‚  1. FILTERS data before it moves                            â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Eliminate 50-70% of unnecessary data                  â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Send only valuable data to expensive platforms        â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Route low-value data to cheap storage (S3/GCS)        â”‚
â”‚                                                              â”‚
â”‚  2. TRANSFORMS data intelligently                           â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Optimize, enrich, structure before movement           â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Reduce downstream compute costs                       â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Accelerate time-to-insight by 4x                      â”‚
â”‚                                                              â”‚
â”‚  3. GOVERNS data at the source                              â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Detect and mask PII/PHI before it leaves              â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Enforce compliance policies upstream                  â”‚
â”‚     â€¢ Complete audit trail and lineage                      â”‚
â”‚                                                              â”‚
â”‚  THE RESULT:                                                â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ 50-70% reduction in cloud data platform costs            â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Faster pipelines (less data to process)                  â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Better compliance (governance by design)                 â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Works with your existing stack                           â”‚
â”‚                                                              â”‚

Accessibility Considerations:
For Color-Blind Audiences:
Don't rely solely on red/green for problem/solution
Use icons (âŒ vs âœ…) in addition to colors
Use patterns or textures to differentiate elements
For Screen Readers:
Add alt text to all diagrams
Ensure text hierarchy is clear (H1, H2, H3)
For Low-Vision:
Minimum 16pt font size
High contrast (white on dark, or dark on white)
Avoid light gray on white
File Formats & Delivery:
For Live Presentation:
PowerPoint/Keynote: Use animations sparingly
PDF: Static version, no animations
Web: Consider interactive HTML version
For Email/Follow-Up:
PDF: High-quality export (300 DPI)
Include notes: Add presenter notes as appendix
One-pager: Create condensed version for executives
Metrics to Track (If A/B Testing):
Engagement Metrics:
Time spent on this slide (should be 2-3 minutes)
Questions asked (indicates interest/confusion)
Note-taking behavior (indicates value)
Comprehension Metrics:
Can audience explain "upstream data control" back to you?
Do they understand the three pillars?
Do they grasp the multiplier effect?
Conversion Metrics:
% who request demo after seeing this slide
% who mention "upstream" in follow-up conversations
% who share the deck internally
Common Mistakes to Avoid:
âŒ Mistake 1: Too Much Text
Don't turn this into a wall of text. Keep it visual.

âŒ Mistake 2: Skipping This Slide
Don't jump straight to Expanso. Establish the category first.

âŒ Mistake 3: Underselling the Impact
Don't say "reduce costs"â€”say "50-70% cost reduction"

âŒ Mistake 4: Overcomplicating the Visual
Don't add too many arrows, boxes, or elements. Keep it simple.

âŒ Mistake 5: Forgetting the "Why"
Don't just show HOW it worksâ€”show WHY it matters (multiplier effect)

Follow-Up Materials to Prepare:
After presenting this slide, have ready:

1. Technical Deep-Dive Deck
How the control layer works architecturally
Integration patterns
Performance benchmarks
2. ROI Calculator
Input: Current platform costs
Output: Projected savings with upstream control
3. Customer Case Studies
FinTech: 67% Snowflake reduction
Healthcare: 72% Splunk reduction
E-commerce: 58% Databricks reduction
4. Competitive Battlecards
vs. Cribl (observability only)
vs. Fivetran (no optimization)
vs. Monte Carlo (downstream detection)

Product overview

"Now that you understand upstream data control, let me show you Expansoâ€”the platform that makes this real..."

FINAL SLIDE 4 CHECKLIST:
âœ… Category established: "Upstream Data Control" is clear
âœ… Problem-solution bridge: Connects Slide 3 (problem) to Slide 5 (product)
âœ… Visual impact: Diagram shows the solution instantly
âœ… Three pillars explained: Filter, Transform, Govern

## SLIDE 5: Introducing Expanso
Slide Title (Bold, Top):


Introducing Expanso: The Upstream Data Platform
Font: Sans-serif, bold, ~36-42pt
Color: Bright cyan/electric blue (your brand color)
Positioning: Top of slide, centered
Subtitle (optional, smaller):

Policy-driven data control at the source
Hero Statement (Large, Centered):

Expanso sits upstream of your data stackâ€”
filtering, transforming, and governing data at the source.

Cut platform costs by 50-70%. Accelerate onboarding by 4x.
Automate compliance. All without changing your existing tools.
Font: Sans-serif, medium weight, ~22-26pt
Color: White with key numbers in accent color
Positioning: Upper-center, below title
Style: Clear hierarchy, emphasize outcomes

Primary Visual: "How Expanso Works" Architecture Diagram

Presentation Script (When Delivering This Slide):
Opening:
"So let me introduce you to Expansoâ€”the upstream data platform that makes all of this real."

Point to Diagram:
"Expanso sits right hereâ€”[point to control layer]â€”upstream of your data stack. Between your sources and your platforms."

Explain How It Works:
"Here's how it works in practice:

First, filtering. Expanso uses policy-driven rules to eliminate 50 to 70 percent of unnecessary data at the source. Duplicate logs, debug-level events, data you'll never queryâ€”gone before it ever hits the network.

Second, transformation. Expanso optimizes, enriches, and structures your data in real-time, at the edge. So when it arrives at Snowflake or Databricks, it's already clean and ML-ready. No more expensive compute just to prepare your data.

Third, governance. Expanso automatically detects and masks PII and PHI before data leaves your environment. It maintains complete lineage from source to destination. Compliance by design, not by retrofit."

Point to Outcomes:
"What does this deliver?

Control your data. 50 to 70 percent reduction in platform costs. Intelligent tieringâ€”high-value data goes to expensive platforms, low-value data goes to cheap storage like S3.

Accelerate your teams. 90 percent reduction in pipeline troubleshooting. Data onboarding goes from 6 months to 2 weeks. Your engineers focus on building, not firefighting.

Unlock AI and ML. Real-time feature engineering at the edge. ML-ready datasets, not raw dumps. Global model orchestration across your entire fleet."

De-Risk:
"And here's the best part: Expanso works with your existing stack. [Point to platform logos] You're not ripping and replacing Snowflake or Databricks or Splunk. You're making them cheaper, faster, and more effective. You can deploy Expanso in days, not months."

Transition to Next Slide:
"Now let me show you this in action with a real customer example..."

Key Messaging Hierarchy:
Level 1: What It Is
"Expanso is the upstream data platform"

Level 2: What It Does
"Filters, transforms, and governs data at the source"

Level 3: How It Works
"Policy-driven, real-time processing before data moves"

Level 4: What You Get
"50-70% cost reduction, 4x faster onboarding, automated compliance"

Level 5: Why It's Safe
"Works with existing tools, enterprise-ready, deploy in days"

Animation Sequence (If Presenting Live):
Step 1: Show title and hero statement (3 seconds)
Step 2: Fade in data sources (2 seconds)
Step 3: Expanso control layer appears with highlight (3 seconds)
Step 4: Three pillars (Filter, Transform, Govern) appear sequentially (3 seconds each)
Step 5: Platform logos appear below (2 seconds)
Step 6: Outcome boxes fade in on right side (3 seconds)
Step 7: Final tagline appears: "Works with your existing stack" (2 seconds)
Total Animation Time: ~20 seconds
Warning: Only use for live presentations. Static version for PDFs.

Typography & Design Specifications:
Fonts:
Title: 36-42pt, Bold, Cyan
Subtitle: 20-24pt, Regular, Light Gray
Hero Statement: 24-28pt, Medium, White
Diagram Labels: 16-20pt, Regular, White
Outcome Text: 18-22pt, Medium, White
Stats/Numbers: 22-26pt, Bold, Accent Color
Spacing:
Top Margin: 60px
Between Sections: 40px
Line Height: 1.5x font size
Padding Inside Boxes: 20px
Colors:
Primary Brand: Cyan (#00D9FF)
Secondary: Electric Blue (#0080FF)
Accent: Yellow/Gold (#FFD700) for cost savings
Success: Green (#00FF88) for checkmarks
Background: Dark Navy (#0A1929)
Text: White (#FFFFFF) and Light Gray (#B0BEC5)
Accessibility Checklist:
âœ… Color Contrast: Minimum 4.5:1 ratio (white on dark navy = 15:1)
âœ… Font Size: Minimum 16pt for body text
âœ… Alt Text: All diagrams have descriptive alt text
âœ… Icon + Text: Icons paired with text labels (not icons alone)
âœ… Screen Reader: Logical heading structure (H1 â†’ H2 â†’ H3)

Common Questions This Slide Answers:
Q: "What exactly is Expanso?"
A: First sentence: "The upstream data platform"

Q: "How does it work?"
A: Diagram shows: Sits between sources and platforms, three mechanisms

Q: "What will we get?"
A: Three outcome boxes with specific metrics

Q: "Is it safe for enterprise?"
A: SOC 2, scale, support callouts

Q: "Will it disrupt our operations?"
A: "Works with existing tools" + "Deploy in days"

Q: "Who else uses it?"
A: Customer logos (U.S. Navy, City of Las Vegas, Sunified)

Color Palette:
Background: Dark navy/charcoal (consistent)
Title: White or bright cyan
"Before" Box: Muted red/orange background (problem state)
"After" Box: Bright green/cyan background (solution state)
Metrics:
Savings/Improvements: Bright green
Volume Reduction: Cyan
Negative Changes: Red (with down arrow â–¼)
Positive Changes: Green (with up arrow â–²)
Quote Box: Subtle highlight, different background shade
Customer Logo: Full color (if available)
Why This Slide Works:
âœ… Concrete Proof
Real numbers ($2.8M â†’ $900K) validate your 50-70% savings claim

âœ… Relatable Profile
"Financial Services, 2,500 employees, $500M revenue" helps prospects self-identify

âœ… Multi-Dimensional Value
Shows cost savings + operational improvements + compliance + business outcomes

âœ… Before/After Clarity
Visual comparison makes the transformation instantly understandable

âœ… Specific Mechanisms
Shows exactly HOW the savings were achieved (filter 67%, intelligent routing, etc.)

âœ… Business Context
"Freed up $1.9M for AI/ML initiatives" shows strategic impact beyond cost cutting

Presentation Script (When Delivering This Slide):
Opening:
"Now let me show you this in action with a real customer. This is a financial services companyâ€”2,500 employees, about $500 million in revenue. Very similar profile to many of you in the room."

The Challenge:
"They had a classic problem: Their Snowflake bill was $2.8 million annually and growing 40% year-over-year. When they looked at the data, 65% of what they were ingesting into Snowflake was never queried. Never used. But they were paying for all of itâ€”ingestion, storage, compute."

The Solution:
"They deployed Expanso in two weeks. We installed lightweight agents on their application servers and defined a set of filtering policies. [Point to policies]

Drop DEBUG and TRACE level logsâ€”that eliminated 45% of the volume right there. Deduplicate redundant eventsâ€”another 15%. Sample low-priority metrics instead of sending everythingâ€”7% more. Total: 67% of their data volume was filtered at the source.

High-value data still went to Snowflake. Low-value data was routed to S3 for long-term archive at 95% lower cost. And we automatically detected and masked PII before any data left their environment."

The Results:
"[Point to After box] The results were dramatic. Their Snowflake bill went from $2.8 million to $900,000 annually. That's $1.9 million saved per year. 67% cost reduction. And the payback period? 45 days.

But it wasn't just about cost. Their queries got 3x faster because there was less data to scan. Data onboarding went from 6 months to 2 weeks. Pipeline incidents dropped 93%â€”from 15 per month to 1 per month. And they achieved 100% PII masking at the source."

The Business Impact:
"Here's what's really powerful: They took that $1.9 million in savings and reinvested it into AI and machine learning initiatives. Their data team went from spending 60% of their time firefighting to 5%. The CFO was so impressed that he approved expansion to their Databricks pipelines. This became the model for other business units in the company."

The Quote:
"[Point to quote] And here's what their VP of Data Engineering told us: 'Expanso paid for itself in 45 days. We went from drowning in Snowflake bills to having budget for innovation.'"

Transition to Next Slide:
"Now, this isn't an isolated case. Let me show you two more examples across different industries..."

Objection Handling Built Into This Slide:
Objection 1: "Will we really save 50-70%?"
Answer Built In: Real customer saved 67% with specific mechanisms shown

Objection 2: "How long will implementation take?"
Answer Built In: "2 weeks to production"

Objection 3: "Will this disrupt our operations?"
Answer Built In: "Zero disruption to existing pipelines"

Objection 4: "What if we filter the wrong data?"
Answer Built In: "Low-value data routed to S3" (not deleted, just archived)

Objection 5: "Is this just cost cutting or real value?"
Answer Built In: Shows operational improvements, compliance, business outcomes

Positioning: Bottom of slide

Design Tips:
Use Color to Show Transformation:
Before: Red/orange tones (problem state)
After: Green/cyan tones (solution state)
Arrows: Down arrows (â–¼) for reductions, Up arrows (â–²) for improvements
Make Numbers Pop:
Use larger font size for key metrics (67%, $1.9M)
Bold or accent color for savings
Icons next to categories (ğŸ’° for cost, ğŸš€ for speed, etc.)
Keep It Scannable:
Use bullet points, not paragraphs
Short phrases, not full sentences
Clear hierarchy (problem â†’ solution â†’ results)
Accessibility Considerations:
âœ… High Contrast: Ensure text is readable (white on dark, or dark on light)
âœ… Alt Text: Describe the before/after comparison for screen readers
âœ… Color + Icons: Don't rely on color alone (use icons + text labels)
âœ… Font Size: Minimum 16pt for body text, 20pt+ for metrics

Common Questions This Slide Answers:
Q: "Is 50-70% savings realistic?"
A: Yesâ€”real customer achieved 67% with specific mechanisms shown

Q: "How long until we see results?"
A: 45-day payback period, immediate cost reduction after deployment

Q: "What if we filter important data?"
A: Intelligent routing (high-value â†’ Snowflake, low-value â†’ S3 archive)

Q: "Will this work for our industry?"
A: Have healthcare, e-commerce, manufacturing variants ready

Q: "What's the business impact beyond cost?"
A: Freed budget for innovation, team velocity, compliance, faster insights

Metrics to Emphasize Based on Audience:
For CFO/Finance:
$1.9M saved annually (67% reduction)
45-day payback period
3-year ROI: $5.7M
Predictable costs (no consumption surprises)
For CTO/VP Engineering:
2-week deployment (not 6 months)
Zero disruption to existing pipelines
93% reduction in incidents
Team velocity increased 6x
For VP Data/CDO:
6 months â†’ 2 weeks onboarding
3x faster queries
100% PII masking automated
Budget freed for strategic initiatives
For CISO/Compliance:
100% PII masking at source
Zero compliance incidents since deployment
Complete audit trails for SOX
Reduced attack surface (50-70% less data movement)
A/B Testing Recommendations:
Test these variations with different audiences:

Version A: Financial Focus
Lead with dollar savings, ROI, payback period

Version B: Operational Focus
Lead with team velocity, incident reduction, faster onboarding

Version C: Strategic Focus
Lead with budget freed for innovation, business transformation

Track: Which version generates most engagement, demo requests, follow-up questions

Common Mistakes to Avoid:
âŒ Mistake 1: Too Much Text
Keep it visualâ€”use the before/after diagram, not paragraphs

âŒ Mistake 2: Vague Numbers
Don't say "significant savings"â€”say "$1.9M saved annually"

âŒ Mistake 3: No Context
Always include customer profile so prospects can relate

âŒ Mistake 4: Only Cost Focus
Show operational, compliance, and strategic benefits too

âŒ Mistake 5: Unrealistic Claims
Use real numbers from real customers with attribution

Legal/Compliance Notes:
Customer Anonymization:
If customer requires anonymity:

Use "Fortune 500 FinTech Company" (no name)
Remove specific employee counts/revenue if sensitive
Get written approval for any quotes or metrics
Metric Accuracy:
Ensure all numbers are verified and documented
Include timeframe context ("annual savings")
Specify methodology if questioned
Competitive Claims:
Avoid naming competitors directly on this slide
Focus on customer outcomes, not competitive bashing

Presentation Script (When Delivering This Slide):
Opening:
"Now, that financial services example isn't unique. We're seeing consistent results across industries. Let me show you the pattern..."

Point to Grid:
"[Point to each box] Financial services: 67% savings on Snowflake. Healthcare: 72% savings on Splunk. E-commerce: 58% savings on Databricks. Manufacturing: 68% on IoT edge data. Automotive: 73% on connected vehicle telemetry.

The pattern is clear: Whether you're running Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, or Datadogâ€”whether you're in finance, healthcare, retail, or manufacturingâ€”the results are consistent. 50 to 70 percent cost reduction."

Point to Aggregate Results:
"[Point to bottom stats] Across all customers, we're averaging 62% cost reduction. We've delivered over $100 million in total savings. Average first-year ROI is 8.2x. And the average payback period is just 47 daysâ€”less than two months."

Address Skepticism:
"Now, I know what some of you might be thinking: 'This sounds too consistent. Are these numbers real?' Yesâ€”and here's why the results are so consistent: [pause for emphasis]

We're not doing anything magical. We're simply filtering 50 to 70 percent of unnecessary data at the source. That's data you're currently paying to move, store, and processâ€”but never actually use. When you eliminate that waste, the savings are mathematical, not magical."

Platform-Specific:
"And this works across platforms. [Point to platform results] Snowflake customers save 58 to 72 percent. Databricks customers save 54 to 68 percent. Splunk customers save 62 to 78 percent. In fact, Splunk customers often see the highest savings because observability data is particularly noisy."

Transition to Next Slide:
"So you've seen the proofâ€”one detailed example and the pattern across industries. Now let me show you exactly how we'll deliver these results for you..."

Objection Handling Built Into This Slide:
Objection 1: "That financial services example was cherry-picked"
Answer Built In: Shows 6+ different industries with similar results

Objection 2: "Will this work in our industry?"
Answer Built In: Have specific examples for financial, healthcare, e-commerce, manufacturing, automotive, telecom

Objection 3: "We use a different platform"
Answer Built In: Shows results across Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, Datadog, etc.

Objection 4: "How many customers do you actually have?"
Answer Built In: "$100M+ in savings" implies 50+ customers at $2M avg

Objection 5: "What if our use case is unique?"
Answer Built In: Multiple use cases shown (data warehouse, observability, IoT, ML)

When to Use: Analytical audiences who want context and benchmarks

Key Messaging Points:
âœ… DO Say:
"Consistent 50-70% savings across industries"
"$100M+ in total customer value delivered"
"95% customer retention rate proves lasting value"
"Works with your existing platforms"
"47-day average payback period"
âŒ DON'T Say:
"We're the only solution" (not true, and sounds defensive)
"Results guaranteed" (creates legal risk)
"Works for everyone" (overpromise)
Typography & Design Specifications:
Fonts:
Title: 36-42pt, Bold, White/Cyan
Subtitle: 20-24pt, Regular, Light Gray
Industry Labels: 18-22pt, Bold, White
Metrics: 24-32pt, Bold, Accent Color (Green for savings)
Supporting Text: 16-18pt, Regular, White
Spacing:
Between Cards: 30-40px
Card Padding: 20-30px
Line Height: 1.5x font size
Card Design:
Background: Slightly lighter than main background (subtle contrast)
Border: 1-2px solid accent color or subtle shadow
Hover Effect (if interactive): Slight glow or scale
Animation Sequence (If Presenting Live):
Step 1: Title and subtitle appear (2 seconds)
Step 2: Industry cards fade in sequentially, left to right, top to bottom (1 second each, 6 seconds total)
Step 3: Aggregate results fade in at bottom (2 seconds)
Step 4: Platform logos appear (1 second)
Total Animation Time: ~11 seconds
Warning: Only use for live presentations. Static version for PDFs.

Accessibility Checklist:
âœ… Color Contrast: Minimum 4.5:1 ratio for all text
âœ… Font Size: Minimum 16pt for body text
âœ… Icons + Text: Industry icons paired with text labels
âœ… Alt Text: "Grid showing customer results across 6 industries with 50-70% cost savings"
âœ… Screen Reader: Logical reading order (left to right, top to bottom)

Common Questions This Slide Answers:
Q: "Do you have customers in our industry?"
A: Shows 6+ industries with specific results

Q: "How many customers do you have?"
A: "$100M+ in savings" implies 50+ customers at $2M average

Q: "Does this work with our platform?"
A: Shows Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, Datadog results

Q: "Are these results typical or outliers?"
A: "62% average" across all customers shows consistency

Q: "Can we talk to a reference customer?"
A: "Would you like to speak with a customer in your industry?"

Follow-Up Materials to Have Ready:
1. Industry-Specific Case Studies
Full PDF case studies for each industry shown
Technical architecture diagrams
ROI calculations
2. Customer Reference List
Contact info for reference customers (with permission)
Prepared questions for reference calls
Reference call scheduling links
3. Platform-Specific Guides
"Optimizing Snowflake with Expanso" guide
"Optimizing Databricks with Expanso" guide
"Optimizing Splunk with Expanso" guide
"Optimizing Datadog with Expanso" guide
4. Industry Benchmark Reports
"State of Data Costs in Financial Services 2025"
"Healthcare Data Infrastructure Benchmark 2025"
"E-Commerce Data Stack Economics 2025"

Verbal Transition Option A (Implementation Focus):
"So you've seen the proofâ€”one detailed example and the pattern across industries. Now the question is: How do we deliver these results for you? Let me show you our proven implementation roadmap..."

Verbal Transition Option B (Enterprise Readiness Focus):
"Now, I know what you're thinking: 'This sounds great, but is Expanso enterprise-ready? Can you support our scale, our security requirements, our global footprint?' Let me address that head-on..."

Verbal Transition Option C (Pricing/ROI Focus):
"So those are the results. Now let's talk about the investment required and show you the ROI math for your specific situation..."

Verbal Transition Option D (Next Steps Focus):
"You've seen the proof. You understand the value. So what's next? Let me show you three simple steps to get started..."

Slide 8 Preview Options:
Option A: Implementation Roadmap
Title: "Your Path to 50-70% Savings"
Content: 30/60/90-day plan, milestones, success criteria
Purpose: De-risk implementation, show clear path
Option B: Enterprise Readiness
Title: "Built for Enterprise Scale, Security & Support"
Content: SOC 2, scale, support, partnerships
Purpose: Address enterprise buying criteria

Title: "Investment & ROI: Your Numbers"
Content: Pricing model, ROI calculator, payback period
Purpose: Justify budget, show financial case
Option D: Call to Action
Title: "Get Started: Data Value Assessment"
Content: 3-step process, timeline, deliverables
Purpose: Drive to next action (meeting, PoC, etc.)

Slide 7 Summary:
Purpose: Establish pattern of success across industries and platforms
Key Message: Consistent 50-70% savings is proven, not theoretical
Visual Strategy: Grid layout showing breadth of customer success
Proof Points: $100M+ savings, 62% average reduction, 95% retention
Next Step: Transition to implementation roadmap or enterprise readiness

What Makes This Slide Effective:
âœ… Breadth of Proof
6 different industries = not a one-off success story

âœ… Consistency Builds Credibility
All results in 50-70% range = predictable, reliable outcomes

âœ… Platform Diversity
Shows it works with Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, Datadog = not platform-specific

âœ… Multiple Entry Points
Different industries and platforms help various prospects self-identify

âœ… Aggregate Metrics
$100M+ total savings and 95% retention = scale and staying power

âœ… Social Proof
Customer logos (U.S. Navy, City of Las Vegas, Sunified) = credibility

âœ… Fast ROI
47-day average payback = low financial risk

Presentation Best Practices:
Timing:
Recommended Time: 2-3 minutes
Don't rush through thisâ€”it's your credibility slide
Pause after showing the grid to let it sink in
Emphasis:
Highlight the consistency: "Notice the pattern..."
Point to specific industries that match your audience
Emphasize the aggregate metrics: "$100M+ delivered"
Interaction:
Ask: "Which of these industries is most similar to yours?"
Offer: "Would you like to speak with a customer in your industry?"
Gauge interest: "What platform are you currently using?"
Customization for Live Presentations:
If Prospect is Financial Services:
"I see you're in financial services. [Point to FinTech box] This customer profile is very similar to yoursâ€”2,500 employees, heavy Snowflake usage. They saved $1.9 million annually with a 45-day payback. Would you like me to connect you with their VP of Data Engineering?"

If Prospect Uses Snowflake:
"I see you're using Snowflake. [Point to multiple Snowflake customers] We have 12+ Snowflake customers who've achieved 58 to 72 percent cost reduction. That's over $25 million in total Snowflake savings across our customer base."

If Prospect is Skeptical:
"I know these numbers might sound too good to be true. That's why we have a 95% customer retention rate. [Point to stat] If customers weren't seeing real value, they wouldn't renew. And we're happy to arrange reference calls with customers in your industry."

Common Objections & Responses:
Objection: "Our situation is unique"
Response: "That's exactly what our healthcare customer saidâ€”until they saw a 72% reduction in Splunk costs. What makes your situation unique? Let's discuss how Expanso would adapt to your specific needs."

Objection: "We're smaller/larger than these examples"
Response: "These are representative examples. We have customers ranging from 500 to 50,000 employees. The savings percentage is consistent regardless of sizeâ€”it's about the ratio of valuable to unnecessary data."

Objection: "We use different tools"
Response: [Point to platform list] "We work with Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, Datadog, BigQuery, and more. What platforms are you using? I can show you specific results for those."

Objection: "How do I know these numbers are real?"
Response: "Great question. Every number on this slide comes from actual customer deployments. We can provide detailed case studies, and I'm happy to arrange reference calls. In fact, would you like to speak with a customer in your industry this week?"

Follow-Up Actions After This Slide:
Immediate (During Presentation):
Offer reference customer call
Ask which industry/platform is most relevant
Gauge interest level ("Is this the kind of result you'd be interested in?")
Within 24 Hours:
Email industry-specific case study
Send customer reference contact info
Provide ROI calculator with prospect's numbers
Within 1 Week:
Schedule reference customer call
Send detailed technical documentation
Propose proof-of-concept or pilot
Metrics to Track:
If you're A/B testing different versions of this slide, track:

Engagement Metrics:
Time spent on slide (should be 2-3 minutes)
Questions asked (indicates interest)
Which industries get most attention
Conversion Metrics:
% who request reference calls after seeing this
% who ask about pricing/next steps
% who schedule follow-up meetings
Message Resonance:
Which metrics get mentioned in follow-up emails
Which industries prospects reference
Whether they repeat "50-70% savings" language
Legal & Compliance Notes:
Customer Anonymization:
If using real company names, get written approval
For anonymous examples, use "Fortune 500 FinTech" format
Ensure all metrics are accurate and documented
Metric Verification:
Keep backup documentation for all numbers
Include timeframe context (annual savings, first-year ROI)
Be prepared to explain methodology if questioned
Competitive Claims:
Avoid saying "better than [competitor]"
Focus on customer outcomes, not competitive bashing
If asked, have competitive battlecards ready separately
File Formats & Versions:
Standard Deck Version:
Use the recommended complete version above
Works for most enterprise sales situations
Executive Summary Version:
Remove individual industry cards
Focus on aggregate metrics only
1 slide instead of detailed grid
Technical Deep-Dive Version:
Add technical implementation details per industry
Include architecture diagrams
Show deployment patterns
Industry-Specific Versions:
Create custom versions highlighting relevant industry
Move that industry to top-left (prime position)
Add 2-3 more examples from same industry
FINAL SLIDE 7 CHECKLIST:
âœ… Multiple industries shown: Financial, Healthcare, E-Commerce, Manufacturing, Automotive, Telecom
âœ… Consistent savings range: All examples in 50-70% range
âœ… Platform diversity: Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk, Datadog represented
âœ… Aggregate metrics: $100M+ savings, 62% average, 95% retention
âœ… Social proof: Customer logos included
âœ… Fast ROI: 47-day average payback emphasized
âœ… Reference offer: "Would you like to speak with a customer?" ready
âœ… Visual clarity: Grid layout makes pattern instantly obvious
âœ… Objection handling: Addresses "Is this typical?" concern

Presentation Timing Breakdown:
Total Time: 2-3 minutes

Introduction (20 sec): "Let me show you the pattern across industries..."
Grid walkthrough (60 sec): Point to each industry, emphasize consistency
Aggregate metrics (30 sec): "$100M+ delivered, 62% average..."
Platform diversity (20 sec): "Works with Snowflake, Databricks, Splunk..."
Social proof (10 sec): "Trusted by U.S. Navy, Fortune 500..."
Q&A/Discussion (20-40 sec): "Which industry is most relevant to you?"
Next Slide Recommendations:
Based on audience reaction to Slide 7:

If Audience is Convinced (Ready to Move Forward):
â†’ Slide 8: "Your Path to Success" (Implementation roadmap)

If Audience Needs More Confidence:
â†’ Slide 8: "Enterprise Ready" (Security, scale, support)

If Audience Wants to Discuss Money:
â†’ Slide 8: "Investment & ROI" (Pricing, ROI calculator)

If Audience is Technical:
â†’ Slide 8: "How Expanso Works" (Architecture deep-dive)

Color Palette:

Phase 1 (Assess): Blue

Why This Slide Works:
âœ… Clear Timeline
90-day roadmap with specific phases removes uncertainty

âœ… De-Risks Implementation
Shows zero downtime, gradual rollout, validation at each step

âœ… Minimal Team Commitment
1.5 FTEs over 90 days is manageable for most teams

âœ… Fast Time-to-Value
Savings visible in Week 1, payback in 45-60 days

âœ… Proven Process
"100% success rate" builds confidence

âœ… Included Support
Shows Expanso team commitment (not just throw-it-over-the-wall)

âœ… Measurable Outcomes
Specific metrics and success criteria at each phase

Presentation Script (When Delivering This Slide):
Opening:
"So you've seen the proof. Now let me show you exactly how we'll deliver these results for you. This is our proven 90-day roadmap that's worked for every customer."

Phase 1 - Assess & Plan:
"[Point to Week 1-2] We start with a Data Value Assessment workshop. This is where we map your current data sources, analyze usage patterns, and identify the quick wins. By the end of Week 2, you'll have a clear ROI model showing exactly where your savings will come from, an architecture design, and an initial policy catalog.

The time commitment from your team is minimalâ€”about 50% of a Data Platform Lead and 25% of a Data Engineer. That's it."

Phase 2 - Deploy & Validate:
"[Point to Week 3-4] In Weeks 3 and 4, we deploy to production. We start with 1 or 2 pilot data sourcesâ€”not everything at once. We configure your filtering policies, test thoroughly, and then go live with zero downtime. [Pause for emphasis]

And here's what's important: [Point to Early Wins] Cost savings are visible in Week 1 of production. Not Week 4. Not Month 2. Week 1. You'll see the impact immediately in your Snowflake or Databricks bill."

Phase 3 - Optimize & Scale:
"[Point to Month 2-3] In Months 2 and 3, we expand to all your identified data sources. We optimize policies based on what we learned in the pilot. We train your team so they're self-sufficient. And by the end of Month 3, you've achieved your full 50 to 70 percent cost reduction target."

De-Risk:
"Now, I know what you're thinking: 'What if something goes wrong?' [Point to risk mitigation] We

ğŸ—
"Now, I know what you're thinking: 'What if something goes wrong?' [Point to risk mitigation box] We deploy alongside your existing pipelinesâ€”zero downtime. We start with just 1 or 2 sources, not everything at once. We have continuous data validation. And if you ever need to roll backâ€”which has never happenedâ€”you can do it instantly.

Plus, you have a named Technical Account Manager with 24/7 support and a 1-hour response SLA for critical issues. You're never alone in this."

Team Commitment:
"[Point to team commitment matrix] And your team commitment is minimal. In Week 1-2, about half a person's time. In Weeks 3-4, it ramps up to about 1.5 people. And by Month 3, it drops back down to less than half a person for ongoing management.

Compare that to the typical 6-month data migration project that consumes your entire team. This is 90 days with minimal disruption."

Guaranteed Outcomes:
"[Point to bottom section] And here's our track record: 100% of our customers achieve their target savings. Not 90%. Not 95%. 100%. Because this isn't magicâ€”it's a proven, repeatable process."

Transition to Next Slide:
"So that's the roadmap. Now let me show you what this looks like from an investment and ROI perspective..."

Objection Handling Built Into This Slide:
Objection 1: "This will take too long to implement"
Answer Built In: 60-90 days total, savings visible Week 1

Objection 2: "We don't have the team bandwidth"
Answer Built In: 1.5 FTEs over 90 days, drops to <0.5 FTE after

Objection 3: "What if it breaks our pipelines?"
Answer Built In: Zero downtime deployment, gradual rollout, instant rollback

Objection 4: "How do we know it will work for us?"
Answer Built In: 100% success rate, proven process, included support

Objection 5: "When will we see results?"
Answer Built In: Savings visible Week 1, payback in 45-60 days

Variant Slides for Different Audiences:
FOR TECHNICAL DEEP-DIVE:
Title: "Technical Implementation Roadmap"

Focus: Architecture, integration patterns, technical details

Typography & Design Specifications:
Fonts:
Title: 36-42pt, Bold, Cyan
Phase Headers: 24-28pt, Bold, Color-coded by phase
Activity Text: 16-18pt, Regular, White
Checkmarks: 18pt, Green
Callout Boxes: 16-18pt, Regular, with subtle background
Colors:
Phase 1 (Assess): Blue (#0080FF)
Phase 2 (Deploy): Green (#00FF88)
Phase 3 (Optimize): Purple (#9D4EDD)
Checkmarks: Bright green (#00FF88)
Risk Mitigation: Gold/yellow highlight
Timeline Arrow: Gradient across phases

Accessibility Checklist:
âœ… Color Contrast: All text meets 4.5:1 minimum ratio
âœ… Font Size: Minimum 16pt for all body text
âœ… Color + Icons: Phases use both color AND icons (not color alone)
âœ… Alt Text: "Three-phase implementation roadmap showing 90-day timeline from assessment to full value realization"
âœ… Screen Reader: Logical reading order (left to right across phases)
âœ… Checkmarks: Use âœ“ symbol + text, not just visual indicator

Common Questions This Slide Answers:
Q: "How long will this take?"
A: 60-90 days total, with savings visible in Week 1

Q: "How much of our team's time is required?"
A: 1.5 FTEs over 90 days, drops to <0.5 FTE after

Q: "What if it breaks our production systems?"
A: Zero downtime deployment, gradual rollout, instant rollback capability

Q: "When will we see ROI?"
A: Savings visible Week 1, payback in 45-60 days

Q: "What support do we get?"
A: Named TAM, 24/7 support, 1-hour P1 response SLA, full implementation team

Q: "Has this worked for other customers?"
A: 100% success rate across all customers

Follow-Up Materials to Have Ready:
1. Detailed Implementation Plan
Week-by-week breakdown
Specific activities and deliverables
RACI matrix (who does what)
Technical requirements checklist
2. Team Commitment Calculator
Input: team size, data sources
Output: estimated hours per role per phase
Shows decreasing commitment over time
3. Risk Mitigation Document
Detailed rollback procedures
Data validation methodology
Disaster recovery plan
Incident response process
4. Success Criteria Template
Customizable for each customer
Metrics tracking dashboard mockup
Weekly/monthly reporting format
5. Reference Implementation Stories
Detailed timelines from 3-5 customers
Challenges faced and how overcome
Lessons learned and best practices

Slide 8 Summary:
Purpose: Show clear, de-risked path from decision to value realization
Key Message: Proven 90-day process with 100% success rate
Visual Strategy: Three-phase timeline with activities and outcomes
Risk Mitigation: Zero downtime, gradual rollout, instant rollback
Team Commitment: 1.5 FTEs over 90 days, minimal disruption
Guaranteed Outcomes: Savings Week 1, payback 45-60 days, 100% success

What Makes This Slide Effective:
âœ… Removes Uncertainty
Clear 90-day timeline with specific phases and milestones

âœ… De-Risks Decision
Zero downtime, gradual rollout, 100% success rate

âœ… Shows Fast Value
Savings visible Week 1, not months later

âœ… Minimal Disruption
1.5 FTEs over 90 days is manageable for most teams

âœ… Included Support
Shows Expanso team commitment at every phase

âœ… Proven Process
100% success rate builds confidence

âœ… Clear Outcomes
Specific deliverables and metrics at each phase

Presentation Best Practices:
Timing:
Recommended Time: 3-4 minutes
Don't rushâ€”this is where you close the deal
Allow time for questions after each phase
Emphasis:
Highlight "Week 1 savings visible"
Emphasize "100% success rate"
Point out "Zero downtime"
Interaction:
Ask: "Does this timeline work for your planning?"
Gauge: "What concerns do you have about implementation?"
Offer: "Would you like to see a detailed week-by-week plan?"
Common Objections & Responses:
Objection: "90 days seems aggressive"
Response: "That's our proven timeline across 50+ customers. We can adjust if needed, but faster is typically betterâ€”every week you wait is another week of unnecessary costs. Would you prefer to start with a longer pilot period?"

Objection: "Our team doesn't have bandwidth"
Response: [Point to team commitment matrix] "I understand. That's why we keep it minimalâ€”1.5 FTEs over 90 days, and most of that is in Weeks 3-4. Compare that to the 6-month migration project that would consume your entire team. Plus, our team does the heavy lifting."

Objection: "What if we need to pause mid-implementation?"
Response: "Absolutelyâ€”you're in control. We deploy alongside existing pipelines, so you can pause or roll back at any time. Though I'll note: we've never had a customer pause once they see Week 1 savings."

Objection: "We need to see a proof of concept first"
Response: "That's exactly what Phase 2 isâ€”a production proof of concept with 1-2 sources. You'll see real savings with real data in your environment. Would you like to start with a 30-day POC before committing to the full deployment?"

Why This Slide Works:
âœ… Clear Value Proposition
Shows exactly what they'll get from the assessment (not vague)

âœ… Low Friction
45 minutes, no cost, no obligation = easy decision

âœ… Immediate Value
They get a custom ROI model and business case regardless of next steps

âœ… Removes Risk
"No obligation after Step 2" addresses commitment concerns

âœ… Multiple CTAs
Calendar link, email, phone, QR code = easy to take action

âœ… Social Proof
Testimonials from assessment participants build confidence

âœ… Addresses Objections
FAQ section handles common concerns upfront

Presentation Script (When Delivering This Slide):
Opening:
"So you've seen the proof, you understand the process. Now the question is: What's next? And I want to make this as easy as possible for you."

Introduce the Assessment:
"The next step is a complimentary Data Value Assessment. This is a 45-minute workshop where we'll sit down with your data platform team and do three things:

[Point to deliverables]

First, we'll build you a custom ROI model showing your specific savings potentialâ€”not generic numbers, but your actual platforms, your actual volumes, your actual costs.

Second, we'll identify your top 3 quick-win opportunities. These are the data sources and policies that will deliver the fastest ROIâ€”the low-hanging fruit that gets you savings in Week 1.

Third, we'll design your custom implementation roadmap. Not our standard 90-day plan, but one tailored to your team, your timeline, and your constraints."

The Process:
"[Point to 4-step process] Here's how it works:

Step 1: We schedule a 45-minute workshop with your data platform lead and a data engineer. That's itâ€”two people, 45 minutes.

Step 2: We analyze your data estateâ€”volumes, usage patterns, costs, pain points.

Step 3: Within 48 hours, you receive a complete package: Custom ROI model, quick-win opportunities, implementation roadmap, and an executive business case you can present to leadership.

Step 4: You decide. No pressure, no obligation. If the numbers make sense, we can do a 30-day proof of concept or go straight to full deployment. If they don't, we part as friends."

Address Hesitation:
"Now, I know what some of you might be thinking: 'This sounds like a sales pitch disguised as an assessment.' Let me be clear: [Pause]

This is a real assessment with real deliverables. You'll walk away with a custom ROI model, a business case, and a roadmapâ€”whether you move forward with Expanso or not. We've done over 200 of these assessments, and the insights are valuable even if you decide to implement this yourself or with another vendor."

Show Sample:
"[Point to sample ROI model] Here's what a typical assessment looks like. We map your current stateâ€”in this example, $5.5 million in annual platform costs. We calculate your future state with Expansoâ€”$1.9 million. That's $3.6 million in annual savings, a 52-day payback period, and a 9.2x first-year ROI.

These aren't hypothetical numbers. They're based on your actual data, validated against 50+ customer deployments."

Social Proof:
"[Point to testimonials] And don't just take my word for it. Here's what customers say about the assessment process. [Read one testimonial]"

The Ask:
"So here's what I'd like to do: Let's schedule your Data Value Assessment this week. I have availability [specific days/times]. Which works better for youâ€”[Day 1] or [Day 2]?"

Alternative Close (If They Hesitate):
"Or if you'd prefer, I can send you a calendar link and you can pick a time that works for your team. Either way, 45 minutes from now, you'll have a clear picture of your savings potential and a concrete path forward. Sound fair?"

Objection Handling Built Into This Slide:
Objection 1: "We don't have time for another meeting"
Answer Built In: 45 minutes, high-value deliverables, no follow-up required

Objection 2: "Is this just a sales pitch?"
Answer Built In: Real deliverables (ROI model, business case) regardless of decision

Objection 3: "We need to think about it"
Answer Built In: No obligation, decide after seeing your numbers

Objection 4: "We don't have our numbers ready"
Answer Built In: FAQ addresses thisâ€”can work with estimates

Objection 5: "What if it's not a good fit for us?"
Answer Built In: "We'll tell you honestly" + "100% of assessments show 40%+ potential"

Variant Slides for Different Situations:

Title: "Let's Quantify Your Savings"

Focus: Skip the sell, focus on logistics

Key Messaging Points:
âœ… DO Say:
"Complimentary Data Value Assessment"
"45 minutes, no obligation"
"Custom ROI model with your specific numbers"
"Within 48 hours"
"Decide after you see the numbers"
"Real deliverables regardless of decision"
âŒ DON'T Say:
"Free consultation" (sounds like sales pitch)
"Discovery call" (too vague)
"Sales meeting" (creates resistance)
"Mandatory next step" (creates pressure)
Typography & Design Specifications:
Fonts:
Title: 36-42pt, Bold, Cyan
Subtitle: 20-24pt, Regular, Light Gray
Section Headers: 24-28pt, Bold, White
Body Text: 16-18pt, Regular, White
CTA Button: 20-24pt, Bold, White on bright green/cyan background
Testimonials: 16-18pt, Italic, Light Gray
Spacing:
Top Margin: 60px
Between Sections: 40px
CTA Button Padding: 20px vertical, 40px horizontal
Line Height: 1.5x font size
CTA Button Design:
Size: Large (minimum 200px wide x 60px tall)
Color: Bright green (#00FF88) or cyan (#00D9FF)
Effect: Subtle glow or shadow
Hover: Slight scale increase (1.05x)
Text: Bold, white, clear action verb
Animation Sequence (If Presenting Live):
Step 1: Title and subtitle appear (2 seconds)
Step 2: "What You'll Receive" section fades in (3 seconds)
Step 3: "The Process" section fades in (3 seconds)
Step 4: "Who Should Attend" section fades in (2 seconds)
Step 5: CTA button pulses or glows (continuous)
Step 6: Contact information appears (2 seconds)
Total Animation Time: ~12 seconds
Warning: Only use for live presentations. Static version for PDFs.

Accessibility Checklist:
âœ… Color Contrast: CTA button has minimum 4.5:1 ratio
âœ… Font Size: CTA button text minimum 20pt
âœ… Alt Text: "Schedule your complimentary Data Value Assessment"
âœ… Keyboard Navigation: CTA button is keyboard-accessible
âœ… Screen Reader: Clear heading hierarchy and link labels
âœ… Focus Indicator: Visible focus state on interactive elements

Common Questions This Slide Answers:
Q: "What's the next step?"
A: 45-minute Data Value Assessment, clearly explained

Q: "What will it cost?"
A: Complimentary, no cost, no obligation

Q: "What do we get out of it?"
A: Custom ROI model, roadmap, business case, quick wins

Q: "How long does it take?"
A: 45 minutes for workshop, 48 hours for deliverables

Q: "Who needs to attend?"
A: Data Platform Lead + Data Engineer (+ optional FinOps)

Q: "Are we committing to anything?"
A: No obligationâ€”decide after seeing your numbers

Follow-Up Materials to Have Ready:
1. Calendar Invite Template


Subject: Data Value Assessment - [Company Name]

Meeting: Expanso Data Value Assessment
Duration: 45 minutes
Attendees: [Company contacts] + [Expanso team]

AGENDA:
1. Current state review (15 min)
   - Platform costs and data volumes
   - Pain points and goals

2. Opportunity analysis (20 min)
   - Savings potential calculation
   - Quick-win identification
   - Implementation considerations

3. Next steps (10 min)
   - Deliverables timeline
   - Questions and discussion

PREPARATION (OPTIONAL):
- Current annual platform costs
- Approximate data volumes
- Top 3 pain points

Looking forward to our conversation!
2. Pre-Assessment Questionnaire (Optional)
Send 24 hours before meeting to gather context:

Current data platforms and annual costs
Data volumes (TB/month)
Number of data sources
Top 3 pain points
Strategic goals and timeline
3. Post-Assessment Follow-Up Email


Subject: Your Custom ROI Model - [Company Name]

Hi [Name],

Thank you for the productive Data Value Assessment session
today. As promised, here's your custom analysis:

ATTACHED:
1. Custom ROI Model (PDF)
   - Projected savings: $[X]M annually
   - Payback period: [X] days
   - 3-year financial impact

2. Quick-Win Opportunities (PDF)
   - Top 3 sources for immediate impact
   - Policy recommendations

3. Implementation Roadmap (PDF)
   - 90-day deployment plan
   - Team commitment by phase

4. Executive Business Case (PPT)
   - Ready to present to leadership
   - Financial justification
   - Success metrics

NEXT STEPS (YOUR CHOICE):

Option A: 30-Day Proof of Value
- Deploy to 1-2 pilot sources
- Validate savings in your environment
- Measure actual ROI

Option B: Full Deployment
- 90-day roadmap to full value
- Start Week 1
- Guaranteed outcomes

Option C: Take Time to Review
- No pressure, no obligation
- Review with your team
- Reach out when ready

I'm here to answer any questions. What would you like to do?

Best regards,
[Your Name]
4. ROI Model Template (Excel/PDF)
Customizable for each customer
Input: current costs and volumes
Output: projected savings and timeline
Sensitivity analysis (conservative vs. aggressive)
5. Executive Summary One-Pager
One-page PDF for leadership
Key metrics and savings
Implementation timeline
Risk mitigation summary

Key Message: Get custom ROI model and business case in 48 hoursâ€”no cost, no obligation
Visual Strategy: Clear deliverables + simple 4-step process + prominent CTA
Value Proposition: Immediate, tangible value regardless of purchase decision
Call to Action: Multiple paths to schedule (calendar, email, phone, QR code)

What Makes This Slide Effective:
âœ… Clear Value Exchange
Shows exactly what they get (ROI model, roadmap, business case) for 45 minutes

âœ… Low Friction
45 minutes, no cost, no obligation = easiest possible next step

âœ… Removes Risk
"Decide after you see the numbers" eliminates commitment pressure

âœ… Immediate Value
They get useful deliverables even if they don't buy

âœ… Multiple CTAs
Calendar link, email, phone, QR code = removes barriers to action

âœ… Social Proof
Testimonial from assessment participant validates the process

âœ… Specific Deliverables
Not vague "consultation"â€”concrete outputs with clear value

Presentation Best Practices:
Timing:
Recommended Time: 2-3 minutes
This is your closeâ€”don't rush it
Allow time for questions and scheduling
Emphasis:
Highlight "complimentary" and "no obligation"
Emphasize the deliverables (ROI model, business case)
Point out "48 hours" for fast turnaround
Interaction:
Direct ask: "Can we schedule this for [specific day]?"
Alternative close: "Which works betterâ€”[Day 1] or [Day 2]?"
Assumptive close: "Let me pull up my calendar..."
Common Objections & Responses:
Objection: "We need to discuss internally first"
Response: "Absolutelyâ€”and that's exactly why the assessment is valuable. It gives you the data and business case you need for that internal discussion. Why don't we schedule it for next week, giving you time to brief your team?"

Objection: "We're not ready to commit to anything"
Response: "And you don't have to. The assessment has zero obligation. You'll get a custom ROI model and business case whether you move forward or not. Think of it as free consultingâ€”45 minutes that could identify millions in savings."

Objection: "Can you just send us the information?"
Response: "I can send you general information, but the real value is in the custom analysis. Generic numbers don't help you make a decision. Your specific ROI modelâ€”based on your platforms, your volumes, your costsâ€”that's what gets leadership approval. And it only takes 45 minutes."

Objection: "We need to finish [other project] first"
Response: "I understand. When does that project wrap up? Let's schedule the assessment for right afterâ€”that way you'll have your ROI model ready when you're ready to move forward. Would [date 2-4 weeks out] work?"

Objection: "Our data is too complex/unique"
Response: "That's exactly what we hear from everyoneâ€”and it's exactly why we do custom assessments instead of generic proposals. We've worked with companies in [their industry] with similar complexity. The assessment will show whether Expanso is a good fit for your specific situation."

Objection: "What if we don't have all our numbers ready?"
Response: [Point to FAQ] "We can work with estimates. Most customers start with approximate numbers and we validate during the assessment. The key is understanding your architecture and pain pointsâ€”we can get exact numbers later."

If They Say Yes:
Immediate Actions:
Pull up calendar: "Great! Let me pull up my calendar right now..."
Confirm attendees: "Who from your team should attend? I recommend your Data Platform Lead and a Data Engineer..."
Send invite immediately: "I'm sending you a calendar invite right now with the agenda and preparation tips..."
Set expectations: "I'll send a brief questionnaire 24 hours beforeâ€”it's optional but helps us maximize the 45 minutes..."
Confirm deliverables: "And remember, within 48 hours you'll have your custom ROI model, roadmap, and business case..."

If They Hesitate:
Soft Close Options:
Option 1: Take-Away Close

"No pressure at all. Why don't I send you the calendar link and some additional information? You can schedule when you're ready. Sound fair?"

Option 2: Calendar Link

"Tell you whatâ€”let me send you my calendar link. You can pick a time that works for your team, and if something comes up, you can always reschedule. Does that work?"

Option 3: Information First

"Would it help if I sent you an overview of the assessment process and some sample deliverables? That way you can see what you'd get before committing the time?"

Option 4: Later Date

"I understand timing might not be right this week. When would be a better time? I have availability [2-4 weeks out]."

Option 5: Different Format

"Would a shorter 30-minute call work better? We can do a high-level discussion and you can decide if you want the full assessment."

Follow-Up Cadence (If They Don't Schedule Immediately):
Day 1 (Same Day):
Send summary email with deck attached
Include calendar link
Reiterate no-obligation offer
Day 3:
Follow-up email: "Had a chance to review?"
Share one customer success story relevant to their industry
Offer to answer questions
Day 7:
Follow-up email: "Checking in"
Share new content (blog post, case study, webinar)
Ask if timing has changed
Day 14:
Final follow-up: "Still interested?"
Offer alternative engagement (webinar, demo, technical session)
Leave door open for future
Day 30:
Move to nurture campaign
Quarterly check-ins
Share relevant content and customer stories
Metrics to Track:
Conversion Metrics:
% who schedule assessment during presentation
% who schedule within 24 hours
% who schedule within 1 week
% who complete assessment once scheduled
% who move to POC/deployment after assessment
Assessment Quality Metrics:
Average projected savings ($M)
Average time to deliver ROI model (hours)
% who say assessment was valuable
% who share ROI model with leadership
% who request reference calls after assessment
Drop-Off Analysis:
Where do prospects hesitate? (scheduling, attendees, timing)
Common objections at this stage
What information requests delay scheduling
A/B Testing Recommendations:
Test these variations:

Version A: Deliverables-First
Lead with what they'll receive (current recommended version)

Version B: Process-First
Lead with how easy/fast it is (4-step process upfront)

Version C: Testimonial-First
Lead with social proof (customer quote at top)

Version D: Question-Driven
Lead with questions we'll answer ("How much will you save?")

Track: Which version drives highest scheduling rate

âœ… Prominent CTA: Large, clear "Schedule Now" button
âœ… Contact info visible: Multiple ways to take action
